Jiangyin 87

Suspected Bandit Remains Under Investigation: The Second Police Station of the South City Gate Public Security Bureau apprehended a bandit named Zhou Shunqi near the City Bridge, who was recording door numbers and household registrations. He was taken to the headquarters for interrogation, where he confessed to joining the party in February. He stated that he was ordered by his uncle, Zhou Lingen, to come to the city to copy down door numbers in order to extort money. He also implicated eleven accomplices, including Wang Xiaomu, Cao Shunpei, and Wang Pei, who were involved in extortion in the countryside. After hearing the confession, Director Li immediately ordered the Detective Squad to cooperate with the Zhouzhuang Defense Corps to arrest Zhou Lingen, Wang Tunan, Wang Guiying, and Zhu Yugao in Wangjia Alley. The Defense Corps also identified three suspects, Zhou Zhanglin, Chen Ankang, and Zhao Linrong. All seven were sent to the headquarters on the 22nd for interrogation, but all denied the charges. They were transferred to the county for further investigation. Yesterday (the 23rd), Xu Qingru, the head of Meian Township, and others, submitted a petition to the county, asserting that Wang Guiying and Wang Tunan were law-abiding citizens, and that Zhou Shunqi was mentally ill and making false accusations.

Response from Provincial Authorities Regarding Embezzlement: During his tenure as the Director of the Finance Bureau, Dai Yuandu and the accountant Liu Muping accused each other of embezzlement, requesting the Finance Department to send Wang Junsun to Cheng to investigate. The petition requested that the Finance Department instruct the county regarding the collection and storage of funds for the Agricultural Bank and the payment of busy season and regular provincial taxes, as well as the transfer of responsibilities to the new Director Shen. The petition also stated that the Public Security Bureau's search was a slight misunderstanding. It also stated that Dai's handover of responsibilities, overseen by his brother Dai Jing, was not problematic and could be dismissed. However, regarding the county party department's allegations of embezzlement, although it was stated that the discrepancy of over nine thousand taels in the busy season of the 17th year was due to outstanding debts, it should be confirmed whether there were any errors in the other receipts. The county magistrate and the new Director Shen should be ordered to respond promptly.

Rickshaw Pullers Resume Work After Strike: Public Security Director Li Zonggang, stated that rickshaws in the city were not following parking regulations and were arbitrarily parked, obstructing traffic. He ordered traffic police officer Xing Lancheng to inform the pullers that they were not allowed to loiter outside designated parking areas. The pullers refused to comply, and on the morning of the 23rd, they went on strike, pulling their rickshaws back to the company. Director Li then sent Inspector Wu Qian to explain the situation to the pullers, and they returned to work.

Local Budget Committee: The County Government convened the 19th Annual Local Budget Committee on the 23rd, chaired by Shen Lunxu, to review the draft budget for the 19th year. Regular revenue was estimated at 176,857 yuan, and temporary revenue at 7,837 yuan, totaling 184,694 yuan. Regular expenditures were estimated at 218,930 yuan, and temporary expenditures at 31,469 yuan, totaling 250,399 yuan. The deficit was estimated at 65,705 yuan. After discussion, adjustments were made to reduce expenditures to balance the budget. The additional tax revenue should be calculated based on the average revenue from the 15th, 16th, and 17th years. Xia Sunhu and Chen Jingzhan were appointed to compile the general budget.

Zhenjiang 89

Former County Magistrate Kong Thoroughly Investigates Embezzlement: Former Zhenjiang County Magistrate Kong Xiankeng, after seeing reports in the newspapers about the case of smuggling opium by ship in Wuchang, where the wording implicated his reputation, urgently requested a thorough investigation of the matter to uncover the truth. It is reported that a section chief under Kong's administration was involved in the fraud, and Kong was deceived. Kong was very angry and went to the province yesterday to meet with Chairman Lai and Director Hu to personally explain the facts of the case and requested a thorough investigation.

Citizens Petition for Opening of Upper Dam: Zhenjiang citizens Chang Dianhua and others stated that the Guanhe River in the city, which flows in from the Jiangkou Ganlu Port, traditionally has an earthen dam built near the Shuiguan to store water for fire prevention, which is an excellent measure. However, because the Guanhe River has not been dredged for a long time and the Ganlu Port has become silted up, the accumulated water has become stagnant, posing a health hazard. They submitted a joint petition to the county magistrate yesterday, requesting permission to dig up the earthen dam to allow the water to flow to the south of the city, thus turning the polluted water into clean water. It is reported that the county magistrate has instructed the Construction Bureau to handle the matter.

Canal Boat Robbed Again by Bandits: Cases of small boats traveling inland from Zhenjiang being robbed by bandits are not uncommon. The robbery at Lujin Town can be described as unprecedented. Yesterday, a small boat of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, towing the Kuali Tuofeng, was traveling to Jieshou Wadian around one o'clock at night when a large group of bandits suddenly appeared and ordered the boat to stop, conducting a thorough search. The losses were estimated at ten thousand yuan. The four box cannons carried by the magistrate of Guanyun County, who was a passenger, were also robbed, and a passenger was injured in the head, resulting in a hole. He was sent to the hospital for treatment today.

New Commanders Appointed to Four Salt Yards: The Huai River Salt Transport Commissioner's Office, concerned about the proliferation of smugglers and their impact on salt farmers and merchants, has appointed Su Zhichen as the commander of the Dongtai Anliang Dingxi Caonian Salt Yards. Qingjiang 91

Huaiyin Holds Spring Relief Efforts: Previously, the local branch of the China Relief Society, due to the continuous crop failures in Huaiyin and the constant rain this spring, which caused widespread hunger, had jointly telegraphed the Shanghai Jiangsu Relief Society and the China Relief Society to request funds for relief efforts. Both societies generously agreed and allocated 5,500 yuan in relief funds. After receiving the funds, the Huaiyin County Government convened a meeting at 3 p.m. on the 20th with the county party department, the chamber of commerce, and various organizations to discuss relief measures. The resulting plan distributed the funds as follows: 1,000 yuan to Xiba, 300 yuan to Wangying (these were designated disaster areas), 1,000 yuan to the first district, 700 yuan each to the second, fourth, and fifth districts, 300 yuan each to the sixth and seventh districts, and 500 yuan to the third district (excluding the towns of Xiba and Wangying).

The National Walking Group Arrives in Pu: The National Walking Group, led by Xie, arrived in Pu on foot from Huai'an at 10 a.m. on the 20th. Hua Shouquan, the director of the Huaiyin Public Education Center, provided all necessary assistance and accommodated them in the center. According to the group, their purpose is to travel the country on foot to strengthen their bodies, promote a spirit of adventure, study history, geography, local customs, language, writing, economics, and industry, to contribute to society in the future and to serve as a reference for academic research and construction. They plan to stay here for five days, then travel north through Liansi to Youyan, and explore Manchuria, Mongolia, Gansu, Shaanxi, Qinghai, and Tibet, eventually returning to Shanghai.

Taizhou 92

Bandit Leader Cheng Wenyu Killed: Cheng Wenyu and Cheng Wenji, bandit leaders from Licheng in the western part of Linhai, colluded with more than a thousand bandits in March of this year, engaging in arson, murder, kidnapping, and looting in the southwestern part of the county. The provincial government dispatched a special task force to suppress them, killing over a hundred bandits. The remaining bandits fled. It is now learned that Zhu Mingtao, the commander of the Fifth Regiment of the Provincial Government's Security Corps stationed in Haimen, sent special agent Ma Lao to lead a team to suppress them. The bandit leaders dared to resist, leading to a fierce battle lasting several hours. The bandits were overwhelmed, and bandit leader Cheng Wenyu was shot and killed on the spot. His head was sent to the Third Battalion headquarters stationed in Mucheng and hung at the South Gate as a warning.

Large-Scale Robbery in Baishuiyang: Baishuiyang in the western part of Linhai has over a hundred shops and is a thriving commercial center. The essence of the entire region is concentrated here. On the night of the 19th of this month, over two hundred bandits suddenly appeared and robbed the area. Villagers, seeing their complete weaponry, dared not resist and allowed the bandits to loot thirteen shops and kidnap Wang Peiqing, carrying away their loot. It is reported that the losses exceed 20,000 yuan. The victims have filed reports with the county government.

Jiaxing 93

Director of Education Bureau Accused: Ren Xuan, the Director of the Jiaxing County Education Bureau, has not made any significant contributions to educational facilities, and the educational content in various districts is also not well-organized, causing local criticism. Recently, the director received a report from Xu Gengmin, a former tenant of the school land, stating that a large amount of school land had been encroached upon. After the Education Fund Committee resolved to investigate the matter based on the report, the individuals involved, upon being summoned, did not appear, causing the case to remain unresolved. Two villagers from Fengjieqiao Township, Ma Furu and Ma Deyou, were also reported to have encroached upon school land. After being notified by the county, the Ma family stated that the land they were currently cultivating had been purchased from the Che family during the Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty and had been managed for many years, with taxes paid regularly. For over twenty years, there had been no disputes, so they did not understand why they were being falsely accused of encroaching upon school land. They hired attorney Xuan Jucao to file a lawsuit in court to claim ownership. The Education Bureau, without waiting for the court's resolution, falsely summoned Ma Deyou to a meeting on the case, induced him to go to the bureau, and forced him to hand over his property certificate. When he stated that he had already submitted it to the court, they did not investigate and immediately detained Ma Deyou. Therefore, attorney Xuan, again hired by Ma, filed a complaint with the court against Ren Xuan, accusing him of illegal detention and requesting legal action. He also sent telegrams to the provincial government, the high court, and the education department, requesting investigation and handling of the matter.

Kidnapping Organization Uncovered in Puyuan: In Puyuan Town, Jiaxing, at midnight the day before yesterday, Tang Shihui, the captain of the First Detachment of the Hangzhou Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau's Detective Team, led several detectives and an informant to Puyuan in the rain. Without making a sound, they rushed to a thatched shed near Yangjia Village in the southern part of Puyuan and searched the area. They rescued a hostage from an underground cave (the person was about thirty years old, wearing a fox fur robe, and said to be from Dayun Temple in Jiashan, who had been kidnapped last winter). Two bandits from Sheng County were arrested on the spot, and a box cannon and a handgun were seized. At dawn, the detective team went to search the Gui family in Puyuan City and arrested two women from the family. The arrested bandits, handguns, and other evidence were taken back to Hangzhou by Captain Tang yesterday for investigation and prosecution.

Assigning Quotas for Construction Bonds: The Jiashan County Construction Bond Promotion Committee, based on the precedent of the 25 Treasury Bonds, allocated quotas to each district at 80% of their assessed value. Preparations for the Provincial Representative Congress: The Zhejiang Provincial Executive Committee, in preparation for the upcoming Provincial Representative Congress, has approved the proposed staff for the Congress Secretariat: Yao Shaoyu as Director of the Document Section, Qiu Xian as Director of the Deliberation Section, and Chou Yue San as Director of the Affairs Section.

Yesterday, the Department of Finance rejected the request, stating that the department was already attentive to the difficulties faced by businesses and that the petitioners were mistaken. Another Resignation of Finance Director Qian: The Zhejiang Finance Director has recently resigned again. It is rumored that the central government has approved the resignation. Another report indicates that the successor will be Zhou Zhenqin, the Liangzhe Transport Commissioner.

Bandits from Qingtian Flee to the Sea from Ou River: The Zhejiang Provincial Government received a telegram yesterday from Gan Qingchi, the commander of the Fourth Security Regiment, stating that the bandits from Qingtian, under siege by the Security Regiment and units of the 135th National Revolutionary Army Brigade, did not dare to cross the river and fled to the sea from the Ou River.

Shaoxing 97

Relief Measures for Disaster and High Rice Prices: Due to crop failures in the surrounding rural areas and the resulting shortage of rice, prices in Shaoxing have skyrocketed. Now, during the period between harvests, impoverished people are unable to eat their fill. The Grain Maintenance Association has purchased over ten thousand bags of rice and has already begun transporting four thousand five hundred bags to Shaoxing for sale at reduced prices. Because it may be difficult to distribute these reduced price rice bags to every rural area, all village councils were ordered yesterday to investigate poor households and report their numbers before the 29th so that rice can be distributed accordingly. There are also plans to distribute aid money, and the county magistrate has ordered all agencies to promptly submit the spring relief funds they have raised. At the same time, efforts are being made to reduce rice prices to benefit the poor.

Stamp Duty for New Salt Merchant Licenses: The case of stamp duty for new salt merchant licenses in eastern Zhejiang, based on the amount of salt permitted, has been submitted to the Transport Commissioner's Office for instructions. Approval has now been received: licenses for less than 100 permits will be affixed with a two-corner stamp, those for less than 500 permits with a five-corner stamp, those for less than 1,000 permits with a one-yuan stamp, and those for 1,000 permits or more with a two-yuan stamp.

Ningbo 98

Loan Established for Police Salaries but Not Yet Distributed: The Ningbo Municipal Government previously borrowed 40,000 yuan from the banking and financial sectors, using vehicle taxes as collateral, to issue police salaries and educational funds. Originally, over 20,000 yuan was to be used for police salaries and over 10,000 yuan for educational funds. The loan was established on the 19th. The Public Security Bureau thought that police salaries would be issued immediately since the loan had been established. However, as of yesterday, they had not yet been issued, making it difficult for officers to manage their subordinates.

Ningbo Educational Community Nominates Representatives to Visit Guangzhou: The Ningbo Municipal Education Association held a joint meeting yesterday (the 22nd) with the primary school association regarding the education study tour. As a result, Wu Shuhuang from the primary school group and Lou Gongfu from the kindergarten group were nominated to go to Guangzhou for the study tour.

Warm Merchants Robbed Near Juexi: In the Dongxi Lingtou area of Diannan Township, Xiangshan County, six Warm merchants were returning from Juexi on the afternoon of the 15th when they were robbed by four long-clothed Taiwanese men with guns, who took more than 1,000 yuan. Lingnan is about five li from Dongxi. By the time the victims reported the incident to the Dongxi Defense Corps, the bandits had fled far away.

Japanese Sailor Drowns: A sailor from Ningbo named Hu Xie Xing, 45 years old, from the Japanese merchant ship Jie Sheng, which was docked in Jiangbei Jiangxin, accidentally fell into the river while working on the ship around 9 p.m. the other night and drowned.

Wuyuan 99

Residents of Lede Flee: Residents of Leping and Dexing in Jiangxi Province have been fleeing to neighboring areas because of the rampant communist bandits and inability to live in peace. Merchants in Leping County have moved their businesses to Raozhou Jingde, creating a critical situation. In recent days, no fewer than 10,000 refugees from Lede have moved into Wuyuan. In the Zhongyun area of the county, carts and vehicles move ceaselessly all day, and people carry belongings on their backs, with children and the elderly moving along the road. In recent days, over a thousand refugees from both counties have arrived in Wucheng, and housing in the city is already full. Those who arrive later live on boats, in a miserable state. However, Wuyuan is already worried about a shortage of food and can barely feed itself. Now that it must accommodate countless refugees, there are concerns that supplies will be insufficient, causing great concern to the authorities.

Quarantine Inspection of Ships from Saigon 101

Cholera outbreaks have recently been discovered in areas such as Annam and Saigon. The Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, in consultation with the leading consul generals stationed in Shanghai, has agreed that all ships arriving in Shanghai from Annam and Saigon must comply with the customs' quarantine inspection regulations, effective immediately. Harbour Master Valley Lane issued a notice yesterday, which is reproduced below. Notice is hereby given, as instructed by the Chief of the Tax Administration, that the Superintendent of this Customs has received a letter stating that cholera outbreaks have been discovered in Annam and Saigon, and that ships arriving from those areas should be inspected in accordance with the Customs' quarantine regulations. The leading American consul general has been notified for compliance, etc. Upon receipt of this notice, compliance is required. All shipping companies are required to comply. This notice is hereby issued.

Municipal Administration Investigation Team of Ji'nan Arrives in Shanghai 105

The Municipal Government is Scheduled to Hold a Banquet to Entertain Tomorrow

The municipal administration investigation team, organized by the Ji'nan Municipal Government and its subordinate bureaus, went to various cities to conduct on-the-spot investigations. They set off from Ji'nan on May 18 and arrived in Shanghai on the evening of the 23rd, staying at the Huizhong Hotel on Sanma Road. The following is a record of the information obtained:

Team Members: The team consists of six members: Secretary-General Cheng Qibao (investigating the overall situation of the city), Xu Dexi, Chief of the Second Section of the Bureau of Social Affairs (investigating social and educational matters), Xu Qianyuan, Director of the Bureau of Finance (investigating financial matters), Li Quanben, Director of the Land Bureau (investigating land matters), Xia Shi of the Public Security Bureau (investigating public security matters), and Ding Qinan, Director of the Bureau of Public Works (investigating public works and public utilities).

Itinerary: They departed from Ji'nan on May 18, spent the 19th to the 23rd in Beijing, will be in Shanghai from the 23rd to the 27th, will be in Hangzhou from the 27th to the 29th, will be in Qingdao from the 31st to June 2nd, and will return to Ji'nan from Dalian on June 7th.

Purpose of Investigation: According to a member of the team, the purpose of this investigation is twofold: one is to conduct a practical investigation of the progress of various undertakings for reference, and the other is to discuss and study at any time for future policy-making.

Municipal Government Reception: The Shandong Provincial Government and the Ji'nan Municipal Government have contacted the municipal government by telegram regarding the investigation of the team in Shanghai. Subordinates May Not Resign When Senior Officers Are Replaced 107

The Municipal Government Instructs Subordinate Agencies to Comply

The Executive Yuan instructed the Municipal Government yesterday, stating that the state establishes officials to serve the people, and it is particularly important to be proficient in performing duties. All officials should be loyal to their duties, prioritizing their responsibilities and placing personal feelings second. To ensure the integrity of public service and prevent abuses, when senior officers are replaced in any agency, subordinate officials may not resign or be dismissed at the same time. It is reported that the Municipal Government has immediately forwarded this instruction to all its subordinate agencies for compliance.

Silver Reserves Decrease by More Than One Million Taels Again 109

Due to the Import Ban on Raw Silver

According to an investigation as of Saturday of this week, the total amount of silver bullion held by financial institutions in Shanghai has decreased by another 1.5 million taels compared to last week. Before the government issued the order banning the import of silver, silver reserves increased by tens of thousands of taels every week. In the first week after the ban was issued, it decreased by over one million taels. This is the second week, and the amount has decreased by such a large sum again, which shows that the ban has had a very significant effect.

Kong Xiangxi's Instructions at the Commodity Inspection Bureau Yesterday 112

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau has been established for one year and two months. Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Industry and Commerce, considers the bureau an affiliated agency of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, whose purpose is to enhance international trade credit and improve the value of export commodities, which is of great importance. Therefore, he has paid exceptional attention to it. He has visited the bureau twice since its establishment and provided much guidance on ongoing matters. Recently, with the successive establishment of the bureau's cotton, livestock, and raw silk inspection offices, as well as the chemical testing office, and with the lace inspection office also in active preparation, the bureau's operations have been developing daily. He made a special visit to the bureau yesterday (the 24th) at 10:00 AM to inspect it. Vice Minister Mu Xiangyue, Technical Advisor Xu Shanxiang, Technical Officer Zhang Jun, and others also arrived successively. Director Zou first accompanied them on a tour of the entire bureau, followed by a meeting with the director, deputy director, secretary, department heads, and technicians. Director Zou delivered a speech, and the department heads reported on the status of inspection work. Minister Kong then delivered instructions, stating that the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau had made rapid progress in its year of establishment. The success was due to Director Zou's proper management and the joint efforts of all staff. "I have four thoughts today. First, it must be revolutionary. All the ills of international trade must be completely eradicated. Second, it must be constructive, so that the achievements of the bureau are new every day and different every year. Third, it must be scientific. Not only should the inspection of commodities conform to scientific methods, but also the spirit of perseverance and long-term scientific research should be used to study inspection policies to make discoveries and improvements. Fourth, it must be business-like. In dealing with merchants, all matters should be treated as one, so that they do not feel they are dealing with officials." In addition, he encouraged the bureau staff with four phrases: "Work hard, maintain credit, communicate business information, and strive for progress." The instructions lasted about an hour. Afterwards, he went to the raw silk inspection office and the silk market to convene all staff members, over a hundred people, and repeated the above points, expressing them earnestly. He also said that Shanghai is a port of international commerce, and the position and responsibility of the Commodity Inspection Bureau are more important than other inspection bureaus. "You come here to work, not only for the Inspection Bureau, nor only for the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, but for the Republic of China. If you hold this spirit and move forward, you will surely contribute to the development of international trade." All the staff members were deeply moved. Vice Minister Mu Xiangyue also gave very earnest instructions. After the meeting, he took a photo with all the staff members of the bureau. He left the bureau at 1:00 PM.

Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee 113

Discussion on the Placement of Employees in the Pharmaceutical Industry

Recommendation of Yu Qiaqing and Others as Petition Representatives

The Shanghai Special Municipality Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee convened a plenary committee meeting for the past two days to address the placement of employees in the pharmaceutical industry. Twenty-three committee members attended, and Wang Xiaolai was publicly elected as chairman. After the formalities, the chairman first invited Party Department representative Tong Xingbai and Social Affairs Bureau Director Pan to report on the process and rationale of the Party and government agencies in handling the case, followed by a report from the secretary on the details of the case, and then a discussion on the following matters: (1) Discussing the placement of unemployed workers in the pharmaceutical industry. It was noted that the hiring of employees is the sole prerogative of the store owner: (1) It must depend on the store's own business conditions, (2) It must depend on the skills and character of the person being hired to make a decision. Only the store owner knows the benefits and drawbacks best. All countries only adopt unemployment introduction and unemployment insurance systems for unemployment relief, because the complete or incomplete power to employ employees has a great relationship with the survival of the store. Since the matter has been in a stalemate for a long time, to seek a win-win situation, it is necessary to petition the Central Government to have the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee and the pharmaceutical industry organizations select those with docile natures from the unemployed workers and do their best to take responsibility for introduction, which is in line with the good intentions of the Party and government authorities to strive for relief for unemployed workers, and it does not conflict with the store's right to employ people. Resolved: Yu Qiaqing, Ye Huijun, Wang Yansong, Wang Xiaolai, Wen Lanting and other five committee members were publicly elected as representatives to petition all parties. (2) The issue of replacement workers in the pharmaceutical industry. After the unemployed workers in the pharmaceutical industry have been given funds and sent back to their place of origin, there are in fact no unemployed workers within the city's area. Therefore, although the Central Government's proposed measures include this issue, it will be handled as a separate case in the future. However, since there is no possibility of implementation in reality, it is proposed to petition the Central Government to cancel it. Resolved: Handed over to the petition representatives for vigorous advocacy. (3) Discussion on the issue of various industries requesting to convene a representative assembly of various industries (A) The issue of various industries' trade unions requesting precedent. On the 22nd, at the plenary meeting of the committee, Party Department representative Tong Xingbai stated on the spot, "I can represent the Party Department in stating that other industries must not demand it in the same way, and the Party Department must not blindly provide assistance." Social Affairs Bureau Director Pan also stated on the spot that the issue of inserting unemployed workers is limited to the pharmaceutical industry, and only to this pharmaceutical dispute. Therefore, the matter of trade unions in various industries using it as a precedent should not become a reality. (B) The issue of unanimously petitioning the Central Government. Resolved: Regarding the request of trade unions in various industries to follow the precedent, this committee should request the Party and government agencies to provide concrete guarantees. As for the representative assembly of various industries, it will be convened again when necessary. (4) Discussion on the issue of protecting human rights. In addition to the temporary chairman Wang Xiaolai requesting the Social Affairs Bureau Director Pan on the spot, promising to protect it in accordance with the law, it was also resolved that the telegram sent by this committee to the Central Government was a gentle plea based on legal principles and facts, and a letter should be sent to the Central Publicity Department, the Garrison Headquarters, the Municipal Party Department, and the Municipal Government, allowing the drafts sent by this committee to the newspapers to be published as much as possible without restriction.

Preparations for the June 3rd Commemoration 115

The China National Anti-Opium Association, in preparation for this year's June 3rd Commemoration, has already contacted and initiated the event with the municipal Party Department and the municipal government, and convened all sectors to prepare for the commemoration, so that the commemoration can be held on schedule, as reported in previous newspapers. The association convened representatives from the municipal Party Department and the municipal government yesterday to discuss the commencement of preparations. The municipal Party Department sent Zhou Hanmei, and the municipal government sent Du Yannan, together with the association's chairman Wang Jingqi and secretary-general Huang Jiahui, to formulate a general outline of measures as follows: (1) The municipal Party Department, the municipal government, and the Anti-Opium Association will jointly request the major newspapers in the city to publish a special issue on the June 3rd Commemoration Day. The materials will be compiled and sent by the Preparatory Committee. In addition to publishing the deeds of Lin Wen-zhong's prohibition of opium and the Premier's legacy, it will also publish the anti-opium remarks of prominent figures in the city such as Ma Xiangbo, Zhang Qun, Chen Dezheng, Lin Shuo, Pan Gongzhan, Wang Jingqi, Huang Jiahui, and other comrades. (2) The municipal government and the municipal Party Department will issue a notice to party departments, government agencies, and mass organizations at all levels to give speeches on the significance of the June 3rd Commemoration during the Commemoration Week (June 3rd) to promote awareness. The Preparatory Committee will supply relevant printed materials and propaganda documents. (3) A Commemoration Conference will be held on June 3rd, convened by the Preparatory Committee to gather representatives from party departments, government agencies, organizations, and schools at all levels to participate. (4) The publication of leaflets for the June 3rd Commemoration and the printing of commemorative hanging scrolls. (5) Holding a June 3rd Commemoration and Anti-Opium Oath-Taking Ceremony. (6) Radio lectures are planned to be given by celebrities on the radio on June 3rd to spread the propaganda. (7) Holding an essay contest is planned to be conducted in conjunction with the city's Education Bureau. The regulations are recorded as follows: China National Anti-Opium Association Essay Contest Regulations. Purpose: To promote anti-drug education and awaken students across the country to study the topic of opium drugs. The following six topics may be chosen, one of which must be selected: (1) The responsibility of colonial governments for the opium disaster of overseas Chinese. (2) The new awareness that the public should have regarding the government's failure to effectively ban opium. (3) The fundamental solutions to Shanghai's opium disaster. (4) The relationship between opium and China's diplomatic failures over the past century. (5) The responsibilities that women should bear for anti-drug efforts. (6) The lessons that Lin Zexu left for us. Style: Vernacular and classical Chinese are acceptable. Word count: Limited to 5,000 words. Eligibility: All students in universities inside and outside of China are eligible to apply. Deadline: (A) Submissions will be accepted until August 29th of this year. Late submissions will not be recorded. (B) The results will be announced during the Anti-Drug Movement Week. Judging Committee: Will be hired by this Association. Prizes: A total of three winning entries will be selected. First place will receive a gold medal, and second and third places will receive silver medals. In addition, if there are good entries, more will be selected and this Association's published books will be awarded. If the essay committee of this association believes that there are no good entries, it may also reduce the number of winners. Application Regulations: (A) Each person is limited to one entry. (B) This essay contest emphasizes creativity and practical investigation. Books cited must be listed at the end of the volume. (C) The text must be written clearly with a pen and should not be too sloppy. (D) The application documents must include the applicant's detailed address, signature, seal, and a four-inch photograph of the applicant's half-body. Supplementary Provisions: (A) Unselected entries will be returned if a preliminary statement has been made and a postage stamp of ten cents is attached. (B) The copyright of the selected volumes belongs to this association.

Ministry of Communications 119

Equipping to Ensure Aviation Flight Safety

Weather Telegrams Advanced

Long-Distance Telephone Reports on Weather

Ministry of Communications Orders All Bureaus to Comply

Since the unofficial opening of the Shanghai-Hankou air route in our country’s aviation industry (the official opening date is June 1st), the atmosphere for development has suddenly presented itself, and the public's interest in airplanes and air travel has increased accordingly. However, the authorities have not yet been able to fully achieve a thorough state of various facilities to ensure aviation flight safety. In order to strive for the development of the aviation industry and the safety of passengers, the Ministry of Communications has decided to increase the weather code to five characters and to advance the dispatch of weather telegrams as much as possible, and to report the sky's weather by long-distance telephone so that airlines and stations along the way can be prepared when the aircraft is flying, to avoid being caught off guard in the middle of the journey and causing accidents. The wired telegraph bureau, wireless radio station and long-distance telephone office in this city have all received this order from the Ministry of Communications and will comply immediately. The charging method will still be implemented according to the regulations for Beijing-Fengtian charges.

Shanghai's Exports to the Philippines in April 120

According to the Da Wan Bao, according to the announcement by the US Consul General in Shanghai, Shanghai's exports to the Philippines in April were even stronger than the previous three months. Among the animals and their by-products, fresh eggs accounted for the most, totaling US$89,173, while the total value for the four months was US$272,235. The second was lard, valued at US$33,704, and leather goods were valued at US$30,544. Among plants and their by-products, peanut kernels were valued at US$5,565, peanut oil was valued at US$10,466, and beans were valued at US$5,190. Among textiles, cotton fabrics were valued at US$22,803, cotton blankets were valued at US$15,186, while silk and satin were only valued at US$5,274, raw silk was only valued at US$942, and grass woven products were also valued at US$1,832. In addition, light bulbs were also valued at US$7,651. The total value for the four months was US$19,172, and photographic materials were valued at US$2,093, and face powder was also valued at US$361.

Jiangxi and Anhui 121

Reply from the Two Provincial Governments to the Anhui Fellow-Villagers Association Telegram

Regarding the Food Affairs of Huizhou

Due to the recent lack of rice and grain in various counties in Huizhou, the public is unusually panicked. Based on the situation, the Anhui Fellow-Villagers Association in Shanghai has repeatedly telegraphed the governments of Anhui and Jiangxi provinces, requesting relief to maintain the people's food supply. The governments of Anhui and Jiangxi provinces both sent reply telegrams to the association, saying: (1) To the Shanghai Anhui Fellow-Villagers Association in Shanghai, we recently approved the letter stating that rice prices have risen sharply in various counties in southern Anhui, and the people's food supply is worrying, requesting that measures be taken to remedy the situation, and forwarding the consultation to the Jiangxi Provincial Government, approving the flow of rice for transportation. Upon approval, before the case was presented, the county magistrates of Qimen and Wuyuan counties, as well as local public groups in the counties, presented it to the government one after another, and repeatedly telegraphed the Jiangxi Provincial Government, requesting special accommodation to instruct counties such as Poyang and Fuliang to transport rice as usual. In addition, the Qimen Flag Provincial Fellow-Villagers Association publicly recommended representative Hu Wei-yin to visit and request consideration, and the case was transferred for consultation. The cause was approved, except for the re-telegraphing of the Jiangxi Provincial Government to approve the flow of rice for transportation, and the distribution of telegrams to the county magistrates of Huining and other counties in the two prefectures for proper maintenance and remedy. Special review and verification of the Anhui Provincial Government Hao seal. (2) To the Anhui Fellow-Villagers Association in Shanghai, we are aware of the letter dated May 9th, and the matter of relief should be handled as required. However, after investigating the counties in this province, we found that they suffered repeated wind, insect, flood, and drought disasters last year, and the harvest was meager. The provincial affairs meeting has resolved to order the Accounting Council to rush to Shanghai to purchase 10,000 stones of Xian rice, and to convene gentry and merchants to raise additional funds to purchase 100,000 stones of Xian rice to the province for low-price sales, and the records are on file. Furthermore, civil food maintenance organizations in various counties have automatically raised funds and requested the issuance of passports to purchase rice in Shanghai. Many have come here. The lack of rice and grain in this province has indeed been difficult to manage and there is no surplus available for assistance. Special reply to this telegram, hoping to be understood, Jiangxi Provincial Government Hao seal.

Hunan Refugees Fail to Move Rice 123

Liu Heshan's Boat Anchors in Dongxiang, Qingpu

Boatmen Sound Gongs and Villagers Gather from Various Villages

Liu Heshan's clam shell-hulled rice boat, carrying 160 stones of white rice loaded in Qingjiao to Shanghai for sale, was anchored in Dongxiang, Biaopu, around 6:00 AM the day before yesterday. Suddenly, more than a dozen small boats arrived and stopped next to Liu's boat. Dozens of men and women told Liu that they were Hunan refugees and that the harvest in the fields last year was poor, making it impossible to beg along the way. "We have a total of more than 300 people in our group. We heard that your boat is loaded with rice and grain. We implore you to lend us a little to avoid starvation." Liu listened and immediately secretly instructed his crew to go ashore and sound the gong for help, while telling the refugees, "The rice in the boat is cargo for customers. I only get paid for transportation. If anything is missing, the owner will ask me to compensate. Please find another way." However, the women on the boat ignored the explanation and opened the cargo hold, preparing to move the rice with baskets. Unexpectedly, the crew sounded the gong on the shore, and villagers from various villages gathered upon hearing the sound. Seeing the large number of people on the shore, the refugees quickly sailed away in their boats towards the South River. Liu checked the rice and found that it had not been stolen, but his own clothes and the crew's bedding had been taken away by the refugees. The loss was limited, truly a blessing in disguise. Rice boats in Shanghai were informed and became wary, and are now discussing defense measures.

Establishment of the Dried Longan Trade Association 124

The meeting proceeded as scheduled. Li Weicang, Fu Zai-gao, Zhou Xin-chu, He Shi, Zhu Pin-fu, Tang Jian-xing, and Lian Huan-tang were elected as executive committee members and were sworn into office on the spot. After the ceremony, tea and refreshments were served, and the meeting adjourned.

Local News Two

Mediation Proceedings 126

Concerning the Zhifu Lane Housing Case

The Great China Company Aims to Settle the Matter

Willing to Negotiate a Fair Solution

The case involving the tenants of Zhifu Lane on Nanjing Road and the landlord, the Dalun Company, initially arose due to eviction issues. Subsequently, the court adopted the tenants' claims, allowing the landlord to reclaim the property but limiting it to personal use. After the retrial judgment, the Dalun Company, being subject to the verdict, originally intended to appeal to the Supreme Court. However, the Great China Company, considering the tenants' claim of established custom and the court's judgment, believed that purchasing the land for self-use would be better than leasing it and causing disputes. Therefore, they decisively prepared the price and purchased the Dalun property, intending to settle the matter and avoid further complications. After purchasing the land, the Great China Company notified the tenants, setting a deadline of the end of May for them to relocate. However, the tenants have not yet responded. The Great China Company, fearing potential misunderstandings with the tenants, sent a letter to the Guangzhao Public Association, requesting them to mediate on their behalf, based on their shared hometown connection, with several tenants, including the China Underwear Company. The Public Association, noting that only a minority of the tenants were Cantonese, forwarded the letter to the Business Rectification Association for overall guidance. Having accepted the request, the Business Rectification Association has sent letters to all tenants, inviting them to a meeting for negotiations. It is hoped that among the tenants, there will be enlightened individuals who, once guided by the Business Rectification Association, will resolve the matter peacefully. The original letter from the Guangzhao Public Association to the Business Rectification Association is included below for your reference:

To the Shanghai Business Community Rectification Committee,

Greetings. We recently received a letter from the Great China Co., Ltd., stating: "Our company has been preparing since its inception for over a year, painstakingly establishing our company, and we are planning to build a commercial center to promote domestic products and contribute to the people's livelihood. However, due to the leased land, the landlord Dalun Company was involved in litigation with the old tenants regarding the reconstruction of the building, causing delays in our company's planned progress. The details of the lawsuit between Dalun and the tenants have been reported in various newspapers, and the public has its own judgment, so there is no need to elaborate further. Currently, our board of directors believes that since the company's commercial center is restricted by the leased land, it would be better to purchase property for self-use to facilitate progress. Moreover, according to the reasons for the lawsuit presented by the tenants in the Provisional Court, they claim that Shanghai custom dictates that landlords can only reclaim property for their own use, and the court adopted this as the basis for its judgment. Regardless of whether the tenants' claim is valid, since our company has acquired the land, even if we fully comply with the custom claimed by the tenants, the tenants should have no grounds to deny our legitimate reason for reclaiming it for our own use. Therefore, our board of directors unanimously decided to prepare the price to purchase the Dalun property completely for our own use. Our company's desire to seek a compromise has reached its limit. We have separately notified the tenants of our acquired property rights and our intention to reclaim it for our own use, requesting them to relocate within the one-month period applicable according to common custom. However, the tenants have refused to accept this, which seems to be due to a misunderstanding. However, several tenants, such as the Nanyang Hosiery Factory, China Underwear Company, and Yi'an Residence, are all Cantonese businesses with established ties, and we hope that they can act fairly and not create obstacles that would lead to extreme measures. As for the other tenants, if they can avoid emotional disputes, our company is also willing to uphold the principle of peace and negotiate a fair solution. We have long admired the directors of your esteemed Public Association for their dedication to public welfare and service to our community. They always strive to protect the interests of the people. Therefore, we earnestly request your esteemed organization to uphold justice and mediate the dispute between our company and the tenants. Within our company's capabilities, we are willing to abide by your fair judgment to achieve the goal of settling the matter peacefully. This matter concerns the interests of the public, and we trust that the gentlemen of your esteemed organization will accept our request without hesitation."

Based on the above, it appears that the company involved is concerned that the other party may obstruct the exercise of their property rights, and has therefore requested our Public Association to mediate. We understand that there are more than twenty tenants involved. However, in addition to those from our province, such as the Nanyang Hosiery Factory, the other tenants have the same relationship. Therefore, they should be treated as a whole and encouraged to pursue a peaceful resolution. Our Public Association believes that the scope of the dispute is broad. Even if one side is resolved, the effect may be minimal. Your esteemed organization, with its leaders and wise men, can concentrate public opinion and conduct fair business judgment, and has a proven track record. Therefore, we should transfer the mediation task of this case to your esteemed organization for handling, so as to achieve peace and settle the matter, and strengthen public relations. This is addressed to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Consolidation Committee.

Chen Mingjian's Actions Unacceptable to His Family 127

Strangled to Death by His Mother and Wife

Mother and Wife Hated His Cruelty and Bullying

Assassinated in His Sleep by Mother-in-Law and Daughter-in-Law

Body Strangled, Carried and Abandoned in the Wilderness

All Admitted Freely in Court

Chen Zhang, a woman from Suqian, due to her son Chen Mingjian's lack of diligence and addiction to opium, separated from him. Zhang now lives in a lean-to in the British Huayuanli No. 1681 on Robison Road in West Shanghai. Her son and daughter-in-law, Chen Zhu, live in No. 1658 in the same lane. Zhu also does not rely on her husband for support and makes a living by working. Chen, whenever he had no money to spend, in addition to using his wife's money, would still ask his wife for money to spend in opium dens. If she did not give it to him, he would resort to violence. Therefore, his mother and wife hated him to the bone and decided to eliminate this evil creature to avoid future troubles. At about 10 pm on the 22nd of this month, Mingjian was lying in his mother's room. The mother-in-law and daughter-in-law took advantage of his deep sleep and quickly took ropes to tie his hands and feet, and tightly stuffed cotton into his mouth. Mingjian woke up from his dream, unable to shout, and difficult to move his hands and feet, so he could only let them do as they pleased.

After a while, the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law strangled him to death. Then, that night, they carried the body out and abandoned it in the nearby wilderness. At first, no one knew. The next morning, Chinese police officer No. 1054 of the Putuo Road patrol station was patrolling the area, and found the body, reporting it to the head of the police station. Detective Ji Liren, detective Ma Zonglai, detective Ma Mouxiang, and Western detective Kataier began investigating and learned the cause of the murder. They went to Chen Zhang and Chen Zhu at No. 1681 in North Huayuanli. The mother-in-law and daughter-in-law were arrested and sent to the women's prison of the Special District Court. Then, the body was transported to the autopsy room on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Judge Sun of the Special District Court took his seat in the second court and ordered the two to be brought to court for interrogation. Prosecutor Xu Mei also attended the court to perform his prosecutorial duties. First, the police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that the defendant was being prosecuted for the crime of killing a relative under Article 283 of the criminal law. Then, the Chinese and Western detectives reported the investigation after discovering the body, saying that at the time they saw rope marks on the neck of the body, and suspected strangulation. There were many onlookers at the scene where the body was found, and one of the onlookers recognized the deceased as Chen Mingjian, and reported Chen's residence at No. 1658 in Huayuanli. They went to that address to investigate, and then learned that the two defendants were both at No. 1681, and then went to arrest the two women and brought them to the police station.

They admitted to the murder without hesitation, and said that after the murder, they put the body in a bamboo basket, and the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law carried it out and abandoned it, but they did not know where the bamboo basket was thrown, and had not yet been found. A carrying pole and a rope were found in the haystack in the kitchen of the house, and they were brought to the case. Judge Sun interrogated Chen Zhu, who stated that she was 23 years old, and worked in a factory. She had recently been sick and stopped working at home. The deceased was her husband. They had been married for four years and had no children. Her husband did not work and was addicted to opium. Most of his wages were spent. She hated him very much. Her mother-in-law, Zhang, was often beaten by him for not giving him money. The court asked who came up with the idea of the murder. She continued, "My husband asked my aunt for money a few days ago and got nothing. There was a big quarrel at that time. The night before last, my aunt called me to her place to discuss how to kill my husband."

"At that time, my husband was sleeping soundly in my aunt's kitchen. Then, my aunt first tied his hands and feet, and stuffed his mouth with cotton, and then strangled him with a rope." The court asked how old the deceased was and why he did not resist at the time. The woman replied that her husband was thirty years old and had been weakened by his addiction to opium, and was also fast asleep. The court further asked where she was when he was strangled, and she said, "I was watching. All the things like tying his hands and feet, stuffing his mouth with cotton, and strangling his neck were done by my aunt. After that, I helped carry him out and threw him in the wilderness. It was deep at night, and no one saw." Then he questioned Chen Zhang who confessed her husband was named Chen Anming and had died of illness on the 17th of the previous month. She had two sons and three daughters. The deceased was her eldest son. He had no occupation

Associated with bandits, and addicted to opium, spending two or three dollars every day. If she didn't give him money, he would assault her. So all my clothes were ruined. I was very angry. That's why I took advantage of him being asleep the night before and I tied his hands and feet, stuffed them with cotton, and strangled him with a rope. I ordered my daughter-in-law to help

Carry the body to be abandoned. I already had this idea last year, and I had discussed it with my daughter-in-law, but it was not carried out." Judge Sun ordered the two defendants to be returned to custody for further interrogation at a later date. At 11 o'clock, prosecutor Guo drove to the morgue to examine the body, ordered the Pushan Villa to claim the body and put it in a coffin.

Deputy Comprador of Ewo Bank Flees with Funds 128

Two Clerks Arrested

Suspected of Collusion

Served in the Bank for Twelve Years

Each Paid a Surety of 30,000 Yuan

Zhu Jixing, the deputy comprador of the British Ewo Bank, fled with a huge sum of 150,000 yuan, abandoning his post. Later, he sent a letter to the bank, saying that he was forced to do so and would repay the money in the future. The bank has reported the case to the police and requested his arrest, as reported in this newspaper. After this incident, the bank's Western employees began to audit the accounts. Now, Xie Tonghou from Ningbo and Yu Xiling from Zhenjiang, both clerks, are suspected of colluding with Zhu. The day before yesterday at 1 pm, the General Patrol Room was notified by phone and dispatched Chinese detective Fei Kelun and Western detective Datts to arrest Xie and Yu. They were taken to the Special District Court yesterday morning to be tried by Judge Xu Jiashi. The defendants hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Jiang Baoli for their defense. According to the police lawyer Gan Jingxian, the fugitive Zhu Jixing had been embezzling from January to May 20 of this year. His method was to replace the collected bank drafts with fake drafts, resulting in a loss of 150,000 yuan. The bank has now commissioned an accountant to audit the accounts. In the accounts kept by the two defendants, the following omissions were discovered: (1) 9,000 taels, (2) 9,987 taels, (3) 1,929 taels, (4) 21,500 taels. In addition, there were silver notes worth 60,389.7 taels, but only 1,500 taels were recorded in the accounts. Therefore, the two defendants are being prosecuted under Article 357 of the criminal law. Next, Mr. Packster, a Western employee of Ewo Bank, stated that Xie and Yu were both employees in the comprador's office. The fugitive Zhu Jixing had served in the bank for 15 years, and Xie and Yu had also been there for 12 years. He was in charge of the Western accounts, while the Chinese accounts were entirely the responsibility of the comprador. Then, British accountant Hardman, hired by Ewo Bank, reported that after auditing the accounts, he found the same omissions as stated by lawyer Gan. When questioned, Xie Tonghou stated that the two account books were not important. He had notified comprador Zhu of the omissions, but they had to see the bank drafts to record them. The omissions were all because comprador Zhu had not handed over the bank drafts. Yu Xiling stated that he recorded the accounts of more than 60,000 and more than 20,000, and handed over the drafts to Huxster. At that time, Pai said that the drafts were forged. The police lawyer then presented a letter, saying that this letter was sent by Zhu to Xie after his escape, stating that 30,000 taels of silver had been returned to the bank, so Xie was especially suspected in this case. Finally, the two lawyers Jiang and Jiang requested that the defendants be allowed to post bail. Judge Xu ordered the defendants to pay a surety of 30,000 yuan and adjourned the hearing for further interrogation at a later date.

Suzhou Elementary School Teacher 129

Frauds in Shanghai

Impersonates Court Clerk

Solicits Bribes for Investigating Sandalwood Case

The Sino-Australian Trading Company on Sijing Road and Chen Maotang were involved in a lawsuit in the Special District Court over the purchase of sandalwood. The opening of the trial has been reported in this newspaper. Unexpectedly, at 2 pm the day before yesterday, Wang Lianzhi from Suzhou, impersonating the clerk of Judge Xu Wenrong, who was presiding over the case, went to the Sino-Australian Company and solicited 15 yuan and 8 jiao from the employee Zhou Xinzhi. Zhou suspected something was amiss and immediately telephoned the Special District Court to inquire. He learned that it was indeed a scam and reported it to the General Patrol Room. Detectives were dispatched and arrested Wang, seizing a diary and a litigation document from him. Yesterday morning, he was taken to the Special District Court to be tried by Judge Xu. Chief Prosecutor Zhou also attended the court to perform his prosecutorial duties. First, the police lawyer stated that Wang Lianzhi was accused of (1) impersonating a public official and (2) fraud. Then, Zhou Xinzhi stated that the defendant claimed to be Judge Xu's clerk and an investigator from the First Division of the court, specially dispatched to investigate the details of the case. He believed him to be true at the time and handed over the case files for review. Wang reviewed and copied them, and said that the trial would continue on June 2, and evidence should be submitted at that time. Finally, he solicited an investigation fee of 15 yuan and 8 jiao, asking to see his identification badge, but the defendant said he did not bring it. When questioned, the defendant stated that he was an elementary school teacher in Suzhou. He came to Shanghai to impersonate a newspaper reporter after seeing the lawsuit reported in the newspaper and tried to cheat the company, but did not impersonate a court official. Judge Xu ordered the defendant to be detained and adjourned the hearing for further interrogation at a later date.

Newspaper Vendor Unable to Survive 130

Jumps into the Huangpu River During Crossing

Fortunately Rescued by a Sampan Operator

Sent to the Ningbo Fellow-Townsman Association for Assistance

Yesterday at 12:40 pm, a young man dressed in rags and looking disheveled hailed a sampan No. 1212 at the Jiujiang Road Wharf, saying he wanted to cross the river. When the sampan reached the center of the river, the man suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide. His body sank, but then quickly resurfaced. The sampan operator, Chen A Jin, managed to rescue him and sent him to the Lujiazui Water Police Station. After being questioned by the police chief, the man stated that his name was Li Jugeng, 26 years old, from Ningbo. He had been wandering in Shanghai for many years, relying on selling newspapers to make a living. He had recently recovered from a serious illness. However, after the illness, his finances were tight and he was unable to resume his old business. He had no relatives or friends to help him. He had no one to turn to and his livelihood was cut off. He was about to starve to death and had no choice but to take this path. The police chief, seeing his pitiful condition, ordered the detectives to send him to the Ningbo Fellow-Townsman Association for relief.

Good News for Sino-American Ice Transportation 132

The Shanghai office of the Toyo Kisen Steamship Company announced yesterday morning that the company's commercial vessels will transport fresh ice between Shanghai and various ports in North China, and San Francisco and Los Angeles. This transportation business is scheduled to begin when the Kinpu Maru arrives in Shanghai in late August. Other ships equipped with ice compartments are the Kinryu Maru, Kinhi Maru, and Kinroku Maru. Each ship has approximately 10,000 cubic feet of ice compartments, divided into four sections, each with temperature control equipment that is not interconnected. The temperature of the ice compartments can be raised or lowered, with the lowest being ten degrees below zero Celsius.

Cattle and Sheep Traders 134

Oppose the Hongkou Market's Increased Levy

Letter to the Public Works Department Requesting Withdrawal of Increased Levy

A letter from the Cattle and Sheep Traders Association to the Business Consolidation Association states: "Greetings. Our association is currently opposing the increased rental fee for the Hongkou Small Vegetable Market to the Public Works Department at the request of our members. We have received a notice from Mr. Wei Sishi, the head of the Public Works Department's Health Bureau, stating that from June 1, the rental fee for the Hongkou vegetable stallholders will be increased by one yuan per stall per month, bringing the total rental fee to six yuan per stall, which is unbearable. Furthermore, prices have been rising recently, and the domestic war is severely affecting the market, causing small businesses to be on the verge of collapse. Even without the rent increase, your department already feels overwhelmed. If the rent increase is implemented in June, it will be even more difficult. Therefore, we urge this association to strongly oppose it to the bureau to avoid harsh taxes, etc. The Shanghai market has been sluggish recently, and small businesses are even more unprofitable. The impact of the current situation makes it even more difficult to operate. It has been found that in May of 1923, your bureau increased the rent for the Hongkou Vegetable Market because the market was newly built and required a large amount of money, which was the reason for the rent increase. The vegetable market is still the same vegetable market built that year. Rent was already increased in that year, and there is no reason to increase rent now. In view of the fact that rent cannot be increased for these reasons, please consider the difficulties of the merchants and withdraw the decision to increase rent. All rental items for Hongkou vegetable stalls should be collected as before in order to please the merchants. Today, the group is angry and see the rent increase as a hindrance to business, and we are writing to you especially, requesting that your association write to the Public Works Department's chief and the Health Bureau and the Donation Office to avoid increasing the rent for the vegetable market. Shanghaie Special City Cattle and Sheep Association Permanent Commissioner Chen Guanghai."

French Police Prohibit Drug Pills 138

The headquarters of the drug pills has a cellar

Secret Arrest Without Success

The French Concession authorities, in view of the prevalence of drug pills (commonly known as "gun cigarette quitting pills") in the Concession in recent years, have ordered all police stations to strictly prohibit them and secretly investigate the source of the drug pills in order to eradicate them at the root. According to the reporter, the place is heavily guarded, and there are many secret installations in the house. There is a cellar, and it is not easy to crack one layer.

Dachang Town 139

Judgment on the Counterfeit Money Case

Three Criminals Sentenced to Imprisonment Separately

Twelve Counterfeit Banknotes Confiscated

At about 8 am on the morning of the day before yesterday, in Dachang Town, northwest of Wusong, a man wearing a military uniform and two men in plain clothes bought four bars of soap at the Risheng Sundries Store on Che Street. The man in military uniform took out a five-yuan banknote from the Central Bank to pay. The shop clerk recognized it as a counterfeit, so he refused to accept it. The transaction did not take place, and the police on duty nearby noticed and arrested the three men. After a brief interrogation at the police station, they identified themselves as Ye Chunbao, Zhang Guichen, and Wang Guisheng. Eight counterfeit five-yuan banknotes were found in Wang's pocket, and a forged official document and four counterfeit five-yuan banknotes were found on Ye Chunbao. The head of the branch station, Gu Shuxian, determined that the case of using counterfeit money was a criminal case and sent the three criminals to the Baoshan County Public Security Bureau for investigation by the county government. At 1 pm yesterday, Judge Zhang opened the court for interrogation. Ye Chunbao confessed that he was 30 years old, from Shanghai, and a painter. He had been a soldier in the 21st Division. The symbols and uniforms were all worn when he was a soldier. He had now been discharged. As for the origin of the banknotes, he borrowed them from a friend, Yang Guilin, because he was in financial difficulties. Yang gave him 12 five-yuan banknotes, but he did not know whether they were genuine or not. The rest of his confession was evasive. Zhang Guichen was then questioned, and he confessed that he was 22 years old, from Shanghai, and worked as a car dealer. Wang Guisheng was his friend, and he did not know Ye Chunbao. He knew nothing about the use of counterfeit money and begged for mercy. Wang Guisheng was then questioned, and he confessed that he was 16 years old, from Suzhou. Zhang Guichen was his friend, and Yang Guilin gave him the banknotes to use jointly with Zhang Guichen. After reviewing the confessions, Judge Zhang sentenced Ye Chunbao to one year of imprisonment for forging official documents, a fine of two yuan for publicly wearing the uniform of a public official of the Republic of China, and six years of imprisonment for using counterfeit currency, with deprivation of civil rights for six years, to be executed concurrently for a total of six years and two months. Wang Guisheng and Zhang Guichen were each sentenced to six years of imprisonment for jointly using counterfeit currency. The twelve five-yuan banknotes, totaling sixty yuan, and the uniforms and official document symbols were confiscated.

The Case of Zhu Songzhou's Theft 140

Zhu Songzhou Lost More Than 500 Yuan

His Wife's Younger Brother is Accused as a Suspect

Zhu Songzhou, who works in political circles, came to Shanghai for official business on the 7th of last month and stayed in Room 52 of the Yipinxiang Hotel. On the evening of the 10th, when Zhu returned to the hotel from outside, he discovered that more than 500 yuan in cash had been stolen. When he asked the waiter, he said that after Zhu went out, Zhu's friend Chen Abing, also known as Zhou Xijun, came to visit and sat alone in Zhu's room. Only after the friend left did Zhu report it to the police and request the Special District Court to issue a warrant for investigation and arrest. Chen Abing surrendered himself to the Zhabei Police Station the day before yesterday. He was escorted to the court yesterday, where Judge Xu interrogated him. According to Zhu's statement, Chen is his wife's younger brother, but they no longer interact due to his improper behavior. That day, taking advantage of his absence, he broke into the room and stole 500 yuan in cash and 2 yuan and 20 jiao in coins, and a coat. He requested that he be interrogated. The waiter No. 9 of the hotel testified that the defendant was indeed left alone in Zhu's room for a long time that day. Chen denied the theft and said that his sister was the plaintiff's lover and that there was a family dispute in this situation. The court ordered the defendant to post bail of 600 yuan and adjourned the hearing for further interrogation.

Report on the Trial of the House Collapse Injury Case 146

Due to the careless demolition of an old house in the central section of Penglai Road in this city, the adjacent Guodai Building suddenly collapsed, instantly killing thirteen-year-old apprentice Zhang Ada. This tragic incident occurred at 10:00 AM on the 3rd of this month. The local police station detained and sent Huang Yungen, the carpentry foreman, to the District Court for interrogation and detention. It is now known that the case has been prosecuted, and Judge Shao, along with Prosecutor Li, held a trial in the Fifth Court yesterday morning. The defendant, Huang Yungen, hired lawyer Zhu Shuzhen to represent him in court. According to Huang Yungen's testimony, he is thirty-four years old, resides in a sugar lane, and operates under the Huang Yunji construction brand. The Zhu family's house in question, which collapsed on April 12th, belonged to the Education Bureau and was adjacent to the old house being demolished. At the time, they were not demolishing the house; the old house had already been demolished, and they were only removing the adjacent brick wall when the Education Bureau's house suddenly collapsed. He was not present at the scene. He further stated that this type of work was subcontracted to a Mr. Chen. The judge asked if he should have taken precautions for the neighboring house and if there were any dangers when demolishing the wall. Huang replied that because the collapsed house was also a new house, there was no need for support. If it had been an old house, they would have made preparations. When asked how many people were injured or killed, Huang replied that only one apprentice, Zhang Ada, was crushed to death. Zhang Wu, the mother of the deceased, testified that she was thirty-six years old, a local resident living in Nanxiaoshao, Beicaizhen, Pudong. Her son, Ada, was adopted by Huang Yungen as a godson and was learning the trade at Huang's place. The tragic crushing death had nothing to do with Huang, and she requested the judge to show kindness and drop the charges, as Huang was truly wronged. At this point, the defendant's lawyer argued that the defendant carried out all procedures for the construction of this house in accordance with precedents and without any negligence. The responsibility rested with the foreman subcontracted by the Education Bureau for the adjacent house. Although the exterior wall of the collapsed house was ten inches thick, the interior was only five inches thick, and there was no mortar under the wall. Moreover, there were no pillars under the collapsed gatehouse. According to precedents, eight pillars, or at least four, were required. This was unprecedented and requested the court to investigate the facts with the Public Works Bureau and to personally visit the site to clarify the truth. The judge granted the request, ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody, and scheduled a further hearing after investigation.

The Embarrassing Plight of a Matchmaker 159

Not Prepared Sixteen Catties of Meat

Beaten Until His Eyes and Nose Bled

There is a Yang family, from Jiangbei, in front of the Xin Puyu Hall on Guohuo Road, Nanshi, whose daughter is betrothed to the Zhao family, who lives in Zhabei. The wedding was scheduled for yesterday. The day before was the bridal makeup ceremony. According to Jiangbei customs, the groom's family must prepare sixteen catties of pork, ten catties of jellyfish, one catty of dried mussels, and six yuan in cash so that the bride's family can share the meat and vegetables. The cash is used to buy wine. From the day of the bridal makeup, the bride cannot eat or drink. She can only eat two days after the wedding. After eating, she must excrete, but she cannot excrete in her parents' home, nor in the new chamber pot in the husband's home. She must wait until the second day to excrete. So the day before yesterday, the bride slept alone in bed, only eating a few dates to satisfy her hunger. Because she was hungry, she could not take care of the matters of leaving the boudoir at home, and entrusted everything to relatives living with her. Because they have lived in Shanghai for a long time, the groom's family believed that the matter of the sixteen catties of meat in Jiangbei customs could be exempted, so they did not prepare anything. The matchmaker Zhao (the groom's uncle) brought people to the bride's house to pick up the makeup, causing many relatives of the bride to be angry, believing that the groom's family deliberately looked down on the bride's relatives, so they twisted him to the teahouse to reason. The matchmaker was slapped and punched by a group of men and women, and his eyes and nose were bleeding. He refused to go to the police station with the police, but fled for his life. To this day, he does not dare to go to the bride's house again, so he asked someone to act as his agent yesterday. It is a truly amusing story.

Yangjia Canal 160

Male Corpse Drifts in from the Canal

Hands and Feet Bound with Hemp Rope

Drowned After Being Thrown into the River

A nameless male corpse suddenly drifted into the Yangjia Canal near Qian Langzhong Bridge, Donggou Town, Pudong, on the 6th of the current month. The chief of the Fifth Precinct of the Third District of the Municipal Public Safety Bureau ordered the local bailiff to report to the District Court, which appointed a prosecutor to go to the countryside to examine the corpse. However, no family members have claimed the body, so it remains an unsolved case. The District Court believes that because the murderer has not been apprehended, the case cannot be solved, and the dead person will ultimately die with injustice. Therefore, it sent a document to the Municipal Public Safety Bureau yesterday, instructing all districts and teams to urgently apprehend the murderer and investigate the case.

Opposition 163

Labor and Management Mediation Department Established in Concessions

Second District Party Headquarters Issued Declaration Yesterday

The Executive Committee of the Second District of the Municipal Government, yesterday, upon hearing that the concession authorities are now planning to organize a labor and management mediation department, deeply believes that this kind of organization infringes upon national sovereignty and has issued a declaration severely opposing it. The declaration states: (omitted above) Upon hearing that the concession authorities in this city are planning to establish a labor and management mediation department to handle labor and management disputes within the concessions, this committee is extremely alarmed. Investigations reveal that the central government has already promulgated handling laws for labor and management disputes, and these have been revised and promulgated once. All labor and management disputes within our country should abide by these laws and be handled by the competent government. No other labor and management mediation or arbitration organizations are allowed to disrupt our national sovereign rights. It is recalled that last July, the Economic Group and the Chamber of Commerce, both controlled by the concession authorities, advocated for the establishment of a labor and management mediation department. However, this was stopped after opposition from the municipal party and government organs, as well as various organizations. Barely a year has passed, and the absurd idea has been revived, attempting to rekindle the ashes and establish this kind of monstrous and incongruous organization. Examining their intentions, it is clear that they merely seek to achieve their sinister and treacherous schemes and consolidate their foundation of aggression. This committee deeply believes that this action directly disregards our national government and undermines our governance. It is hoped that all comrades and compatriots in the city will unite in opposition, uphold national prestige, and protect national sovereignty. This is hereby declared. The Second District Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Committee of the Kuomintang of China.

Li Guangyuan Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment 164

Li Guangyuan, who worked at the Central Automobile Company on Beile Road in the New Concession, gathered a crowd to cause trouble at the intersection of Kangti Road on March 16th, and threw stones to smash a public bus. Patrol officer number 365 arrived and arrested Li Guangyuan and more than ten others, taking them to the French Concession Court for questioning. The charges were confirmed and the defendants were sentenced to one year in prison as a warning. Because Li Guangyuan appealed the initial judgment, he hired lawyer Fei Xizhen to request a retrial, which was approved by the Chinese and Western officials. The retrial was held yesterday. According to the retrial plaintiff's lawyer, the defendant had always been a law-abiding businessman. On that day, he saw a large number of young men and women shouting slogans in the Kangti Road area. Due to his curiosity, he went out to watch and was mistakenly arrested by the patrol officers. The sentence under Article 157 of the Criminal Law in the initial trial was not applicable. He requested a change and asked for the defendant to be released. Patrol officer 365 stated that he saw Li Guangyuan smashing the bus windows with stones, so he arrested him. The Chinese and Western officials, considering that the defendant was a first-time offender, leniently changed the sentence to six months imprisonment as a warning.
